		<shortDescription>Not really that good</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>With little REAL emotion or even very interesting lines, Three Kings basically hinges on it's graphic war scenes to pull the movie through. Originally touted as a comedy, after about half an hour, your smile fades and the jokes stop. It then focuses on the "story" for the rest of the time, abandoning whatever mood and atmosphere they had previously established. The thing about Three Kings is, there really is no story. Often contradicting and overly tripe, it treats the audience as children, not letting them have any opinions whatsoever. All we're left with is a visual style that we hope brings justice to the Gulf War. It has it's interesting parts, like a new cross-cutting way to show quick, rushed, battle scenes, and an interesting explanation of the bile buildup after one is shot. Three Kings is a stylish film, if not substance driven, and certainly not the best Gulf War movie. Too many are forgetting the four star masterpiece Courage Under Fire with Denzel Washington and Meg Ryan that was released in 1995. That does more justice to the Gulf War than Three Kings does. If you want to see a new breed of modern film making, check Three Kings out. But don't expect to see anything deep, and really don't expect a decent soundtrack.</fullReview>

		<username>(decarch@erols.com)</username>

		<shortDescription>Painfully stupid farcical war "documentary"</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>What is all the fuss about? I heard this movie was "patriotic" and "innovative", etc. I went to see this movie against my will. I saw a preview and thought it looked stupid. I saw a trailer and thought it looked ludicrous and gratuitous. But my husband wanted to see it because he heard all kinds of raving reviews. Now I'm raving--mad. He wanted to leave halfway through the movie but I made him watch through to the end so we'd remember not to spend $17 without trusting our instincts again. And we squirmed in our seats. I had to laugh incredulously (when I wasn't groaning) at nearly every scene. The portrayal of the U.S. military was anything BUT patriotic. It made us look foolish. The opening scene was a huge frat party. Several of the soldiers we meet are dumber than dirt and trigger happy. Sad to see our military men portrayed as so incompetent. Scary! Characters were cardboard cut-out cliches, very flat and superficial. Writing was very amateurish, as if done by a teenage boy for a creative writing class where logic in the plot doesn't matter but machismo does. We meet Archie (Clooney) when he's banging a cute war correspondent in a raunchy, gratuitous sex scene. Of course, they're caught in the act and he gets reprimanded, while the nymphette gets into a catfight with an aging, self-conscious and perpetual Emmy losing reporter, Adriana. I hoped her cranky, one-dimensional character would get abducted by the Iraqis and tortured with Palmolive soap in the mouth, considering every other word out of her mouth was a variation of f***. So the flimsy plot progresses thus: several soldiers find a map tucked just so in the butt of an Iraqi prisoner (insert gratuitous butt humor here). Where were Beavis and Butthead during all this? Or actually, Cornholio? Anyway, Archie finds out about it and convinces the three incompetents that they can use the map to find a secret bunker where Saddam stashed gold bullion stolen from Kuwait. They could bring some back (and "quit their day jobs"). How is this supposed to work? How do four guys go AWOL armed with a few guns and a ceasefire agreement in hand into foreign- speaking enemy territory, breaking into guarded bunkers at gunpoint? Once they find the gold, if they can, how do they bring it back and cash it in without anyone knowing? What bank would give cash value for stolen foreign gold bullion? DOES THIS MAKE SENSE? So the treasure hunters manage to find the gold after schoolmaster Archie lets the boys shoot a few rounds for fun before they encounter a cow in the middle of the desert which is (gratuitously) blown up by a cluster bomb. How did that happen? They steal a truck to load ALL of the gold into. Then they argue about whether to take some refugees with them (since that wasn't the original mission) in a reluctant humanitarian effort to save the Iraqi citizens from the soldiers who try to quell their rebellion. Our golddigger/heroes encounter all kinds of dangerous mishaps with these refugees in tow. Everyone carries some heavy gold through the scorching desert as they try to escape without the vehicles (which got blown up/crashed, of course). One "hero" gets captured and tortured while forced to wear a fancy suit. He also managed to call his wife from a cell phone he found in a box of stolen goods. Clever. More mishaps occur and more refugees join the entourage as this expedition goes haywire and beyond ridiculous. A portrait of Saddam is seen wearing the cap and gown of a college graduate, further confusing the tone of the film. Are we supposed to feel empathy for the slaughtered Iraqis as we see them gunned down by their own army or are we supposed to laugh at the silly tongue- in-cheek portrait of Saddam? And how come Archie thinks he can spend the gold when it belongs to Kuwait? Was the purchase of a fleet of luxury vehicles to fight Saddam's army just an opportunity for product placement by Infiniti, Mercedes-Benz, Lexus, etc.? Or was this an opportunity for a clever ruse just barely pulled off in the script? Several okay ideas were (predictably) used such as nerf football bombs, and some scenes were creatively shot with well-composed stills and grainy "documentary" style camera footage, though this was more effectively used in Saving Private Ryan, especially considering the camera technologies relative to the Gulf War and WWII decades. Other scenes, while meant to be creative and clever, were just plain cartoonish and gross, like the body "x-rays" showing what happens when someone is hit by a bullet. (Minor spoiler:) And how does one survive a gunshot wound to the lung if a clavicle wound can be fatal? Nothing makes sense. I know I'm supposed to appreciate the change of heart and self-realization the pseudoheroes experience but it doesn't work. If the film was intended to show the consequences of a country at war with itself and to show the dire situation of an oppressed and tyrannized people, there's a better way to do it which would elicit more compassion than to undermine their tragic situation with slapstick nonsense and gratuitous camera tricks. War movie humor may work in Life is Beautiful in its heartbreaking attempt to save a little boy from the horrors of a concentration camp,</fullReview>

		<date>2006-07-12</date>
		<username>Randall Cameron</username>
		<score>0.5</score>
		<shortDescription>Four soldiers go AWOL to steal gold after the first Gulf War</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>May contain spoilers!!! Sorry to break up the chorus of rave reviews.Three Kings has terrific production values (photography, cinematography, effects), and I am a Clooney fan. The Arab characters also made sense (reasonably fair portrayal rather than stick figures), although more generous subtitles would probably be nice for non-Arabic speaking audiences. And the self-promoting TV journalists, although caricatures, were not far off the mark.But it flunks too many believability tests (kind of like the TV show Alias). Majors do not even socialize with non-coms, and are unlikely to go off on a criminal venture together before discharge, because of issues of trust. Four (non-Arabic speaking) guys are just going to wander through post-war southern Iraq? They would be quickly killed by the first combatants they met on either side, and the bodies would not even be recovered. End of story.The three lead characters, hardened soldiers turned mercenaries at the beginning, are going to develop hearts along the way? I don't think so. Anyone willing to risk their life or a trip to military prison for just money is not likely to know what compassion is. Spike Jonze as Troy's puppy dog, Conrad was the most believable.The "action scene" in the minefield while tear gas explodes overhead was ridiculous. Chasing a fast moving vehicle with a mortar is almost impossible. Airbursting teargas that high would just dissipate it. Mines are rarely that obvious unless deployed by artillery or air (only done in the face of a mechanized advance); folks on foot do not have to worry about AT mines, since people are neither magnetic nor do they weigh a ton. And Iraq's Army would be unlikely to mine its own road. Nor is anyone going to jump out of a moving Humvee just before it hits. The front of the Humvee would be incinerated, but not flip through the air. And the flying machine gun just happens to hit the van -- get real. Very Hollywood. I was waiting for Rambo in MOPP 4 gear to swing in on a vine with an M60 trailing a loose belt of ammo.I switched off halfway through. The melodrama of Troy imagining his wife and child being blown up when facing the interrogator (portrayed realistically, but Troy by training should *assume* he is lying about his loss of family, especially after electrocuting him) was just too much. Incidentally, Troy (not exactly Delta Force) would have wet or soiled his pants after a jolt like that.I give it 5 out of 10. Has some excellent points, but is irredeemably flawed as a package.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Lacking moral &amp; political depth</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>*spoilers* Although the advertising campaign made it seem like just another action movie, I trusted the positive reviews that it was something much deeper. I was disappointed to learn that it really was the superficial flick that was advertised.At the end of the Gulf War, four hyped-up Ugly Americans pursue a get-rich-quick scheme to plunder Saddam Hussein's own plunder. Along the way they realize the plight of a village of persecuted Iraqis and help them to seek refuge from the Hussein regime, giving up much of the gold in the process. This plotline has caused some to celebrate it as a moral, humanitarian message, but this message unfortunately is superficial. Even though the soldiers change their actions, one doesn't seen a significant, moral transformation within them. There aren't deep connections developed between the GIs and the refugees. The "camel jockey" stereotypes persist among the protagonists even after the tone of the film changes.A note about the film's politics: it is more mainstream than folks on either side of the political spectrum seems to portray it. It is not rabidly unpatriotic as some on the Right suggest. Although it does not portray the GIs as John Wayne or Dudley Do-Right types, all the film's Americans are heroes. Nor does it seem to me to be the anti-war flick, that some on the Left say it is. The film is driven by a sense that the Hussein regime is brutal, immoral, and should be driven out of power. Rather than repudiating the war, it implies that the US should have broadened its intervention in the region.I give the film kudos for treading new ground in its subject matter. Unfortunately, it deals with its subject matter on a superficial matter. It's flawed as an action film as well because of its uncharismatic heroes and what seemed like a major continuity gaffe at one point (I may have just been confused, it seemed that the film got some location mixed up).I gave this film a 4 out of 10.</fullReview>

		<date>2000-11-25</date>
		<username>ZachsMind (zachsmind@yahoo.com)</username>
		<score>0.4</score>
		<shortDescription>Yet another war movie for yet another war.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>This was a painful film to watch, both for its flaws and virtues. George Clooney gives a lackluster performance, and fails to help us see why his character perseveres as the plot complicates. Ice Cube shows great promise but his potential is wasted in this film. Likewise for Nora Dunn and most other supporting players. I winced several times, and not at the bloodshed, but how this story was told.The sound track is incredible. I'll give it that much. A veritable cornucopia of fun music from the latter half of the twentieth century. Quite a contrast to the remarkable UNfun of the movie itself.The tale is based at least loosely on eyewitness accounts of events that took place at the end of the Persian Gulf "war." It sheds crocodile tears to the end of noble chivalry, revealing the truth of why man fights man in these dulled and amoral times. However, it tells us nothing we didn't already know. The reasons to take arms are not for justice, but for material wealth. This is repeatedly slapped in our faces as if to convert us. The priest is preaching to the choir. Repeatedly the characters question why they were even fighting this war. They were in the thick of it and yet never understand why. We know why. We know the Persian Gulf incident was fought over crude oil and gold bullion.The tale also attempts to offer hope that despite mankind's unquenchable thirst for wealth and control of others, deep down we all want to be kinder and gentler to one another. However, the same preacher voice doesn't sell this convincingly, and the end result is a hollow shell of a film that does not captivate. Instead it just leaves one sick in the stomach at the very thought of one's own humanity.Are we all like this? Are we all this shortsighted, vain and greedy? Surely each one who reads these words thinks "not I" but to judge the characters in this film for their actions, both noble and savage, we judge ourselves. Would we do the same if the score of twenty three million American dollars worth of Kuwaiti gold were within our grasp? What price tag do we each place upon the loss of life? The loss of innocence? The loss of sanity?The dialogue is melodramatic when it should have been simple, and at other times simply hollow. The poetry is sporadic and not believable, and when more poetic words would have been preferred, we get rot gut. The plot is based on real events, but it is still a hard hook to swallow, and pulls at the insides. The suspension of disbelief should not be necessary for a story that is this true to life.The first actual gunfight is edited in such a way as to give each bullet a pertinence equal to a presidential address. The camera becomes the bullet for practically every blow to the head. The eye candy is tart and sour. It becomes less like a war movie and more like a Punch and Judy puppet show. The message of needless bloodshed is wrapped around us like a head lock and is suffocating. Again, we KNOW. It's pointless. Why drive the point home like a stake in a vampire's heart? The bloodshed is simultaneously necessary for realism's sake, and more irrelevant than the video game Quake Arena Three. The discoloration and affectation of some scenes is a noble attempt to stylize for visual interest, but it falls short and is superfluous. The characterizations are weak and diluted. Needless to say I was sadly disappointed in Three Kings.The film does attempt to answer the questions: Why must man kill his fellow man? Why do we keep having pointless wars? The answer is a simple and pathetic one. Why, for sand of course! For baubles like cell phones and expensive cars, just to toss them aside or blow them away at the next opportunity. We fight for fear of powerful leaders who command us to hate one another and hoard the wealth so that we must remain subservient. We kill one another not only because we can, and because it is easier to kill disagreement with small metallic pebbles blasted at great speeds with modern technology, than it is to realize that every man woman and child on this planet has the inalienable right to necessities, and dare I say even comforts, despite their disagreements of politics, religion and sociality.The question this production should have asked instead was this: Why do we keep making pointless war movies about pointless wars? I think the answer to that question is equally unsatisfying.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<date>2000-02-01</date>
		<username>Blake French (dlfspartan@aol.com)</username>
		<score>0.5</score>
		<shortDescription>Poorly crafted and under developed. Only the last half gives the film life. ** out of ****.</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>THREE KINGS (1999) **Starring: George Clooney, Ice Cube, Mark Wahlberg, Spike Jonze, Cliff Curtis, Nora Dunn and Judy Greer Written and directed by David O. Russell. Running time: 115 minutes. Rated R (for strong graphic violence, a scene of sexuality, and for strong language)By Blake French:"Three Kings" is a good example of a bad war flick. It is getting so common to see great war movies these days, simply because their subject is based on important eventsl. Therefore good directors and experienced filmmakers are most frequently involved with these productions. War movies, such as "Saving Private Ryan" and "The Thin Red Line," are always events for appreciative audiences. As "Three Kings" explains to us, however, it is possible to create a poorly crafted film of its genre.It's never a good signal when a movie's opening sequence features a bunch of young army men partying like wild animals. "Three Kings" contains character descriptions that consist of captions being typed up on the screen. The story takes place directly after the Gulf War. Four military figures, including soon to retire Archie Gates (George Clooney), young newlywed Troy Barlow (Mark Wahlburg), a Troy Barlow wannabe, and an African American religious man named Chief Elgin. All these folks work up a secret plan to travel on a private, illegal mission to a doomed Iraqian town to rob thief Sadaam Hussein of millions in pure gold.While the film opens as a tale about the consequences of heartless greed, it soon turns into a story about the four money hungry Americans desperately attempting to cross dozens of endangered Iraqi pedestrians over the border for safety from the murdering solders.Unfortunately, by the time the film develops values for the characters, it is already too late. Due to the humorously poor development in the opening, and the foul-mouthed, ignorant attitude of our four kings, we never really care about anyone in this movie. The audience certainly doesn't think highly of the George Clooney character. We first view him on screen as he is having premarital sex in an army post with a young blonde television reporter.Another problem with the characters is the script's lack of interesting intent and energy propelling their actions. We first arrive at the conclusion that the characterswant money--but that goes no where. These are characters who we mostly despise and are unconvincing. We receive profane rapper Ice Cube as a religious man--yeah right? That is as bad as having LL Cool J as someone named Preacher in "Deep Blue Sea" and Eddie Murphy as a Holy Man in the movie of the same name.There is a torture sequence featuring Mark Wahlburg in an electrical chair. That doesn't have any impact either, however, because we know such little about his character. We receive strained chinches about his newborn baby and lovely wife at home in peaceful Michigan. But that is so contrived it's almost funny.This is not to state the actors do not fit their roles, because everyone does a good job at the portrayal of their characters. George Clooney is good in his role, performing with dramatic intensity and some emotion. Ice Cube is also quite believable, but seems a bit underplayed by the other actors. Mark Wahlberg is his usual, ignorant self here, once again proving to us that he can't star in a movie without having a scene of two where he takes his shirt off. This type of role is becoming so conventional for him, its almost a shame that he is most likely confusing acting for modeling."Three Kings" focuses on being hip and having a unique style instead of nurturing subplots, writing good dialogue, and forming descriptive characters. The style is gritty, fast paced and chopped up. Even the soundtrack is ridiculously immature. A particular gun battle scene shows my theory perfectly. It is presented in extreme slow motion as we hear the bullets leave their gun with a loud whoosh then hit the characters in dead science. This sequence tries so hard to be different from other "better" war scenes, it actually wreaks of desperation.Another problem with the style in "Three Kings" is the fact that it tries to be so hip and action packed, it ends up lacking an educational stand on its subject. This film does a poor job of explaining to us the informational nuggets detailing the Gulf War. At the end of this movie, based on what the film said, I still had no idea of what the war was about. It is so fast and fragmented, only at mid point does the film slow down and actually allow the audience to feel the emotional depth present. Its not that I have anything against war movies in general, but "Three Kings" just doesn't work.Brought to you by Warner Bros.</fullReview>

It pains me to speak this way of a film made by a director that crafted such wonderfully made films as Spanking The Monkey and Flirting With Disaster. Those films were sides-splittingly funny, while showing us something meaningful about ourselves. This film, while promising to do the same, fails quite miserably. It is almost as if this movie was the worst possible combination of two films the director had in mind. One a touching war drama, the other a darkly comic view of war. Together, it is a jumbled mess that left me and others wishing it would end quickly.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<fullReview>Just watched Three kings again and decided that I'd give my 2 cents despite the film being a decade old and despite America having had another illegal and brutal war with Iraq. Along the way the trio have a change of heart and set about helping a bunch of Iraqi refugees and slay lots of 'bad guys' while doing it. The film is set on the backdrop of Operation Desert Storm. It manages to entertain as well as evoke empathy for its many characters, which range from a gun toting major played by Clooney and a young officer of the Iraqi republican Guard who has lost his family to Uncle Sam's bombs. While the film does try and raise several important issues, it ends up trivializing Iraqi and Arab suffering by showing them either as victims who need to be helped and guided or self-loathing barbarians who would pimp out or kill their own to stay in their masters good books. The central question, as to what US and co. was (and is) doing in Iraq in the first place is never really answered. The excuse given is the invasion of Kuwait; But, the fact that Kuwait was created out of Iraq by the British and is America's cut price oil barrel today, is mostly forgotten. Now I don't mean to be disrespectful, or to undermine the might &amp; bravery of the reserve American soldier, but it would've been much more convincing if those 4 soldiers were high that morning.my Iraqi friends who fled Baghdad recently tell me that American troops wouldn't dare break into a suspect's home unless they were in a pack of 100 GI's armed to the teeth...So unless that scene was intended to be part of the comedy, I say give us a fudging break!The rest of the movie doesn't go far from that impressive action scene.By the way... Just for the record, another hilarious aspect of this movie: It's how it portrayed Iraqi soldiers as mushy pussies who are waiting to get bitch-slapped! When the truth is, any average Iraqi soldier would beat the living crap out of any average American soldier any given day, unless of course the American hero is hiding inside a metal castle! Or you think those American soldiers falling everyday in Iraq are victims of sunstrokes?!Oh, and another scene I just remembered: When they find the gold, they just pick it up and leave while the guarding Iraqi soldiers remain watching TV and listening to western music?!!! Now putting aside politics, nationalism, gallantry and all that macho-stuff, if I personally had that much gold in my possession, I would annihilate America itself to keep that fortune for myself, out of pure human greed! Not just stand there helplessly as I watch 4 homo clowns taking it all away!Yet about the over-dramatic mistreatment of the Shiites fabricated here, this sad excuse of a movie was an early attempt to indirectly brainwash the American public when it comes to picturing Saddam &amp; his regime as ruthless killers who deserve to be invaded!While now it turns out that a whole year of biased trials + endless piles of false documents and testimonies are not enough to convict the man of war crimes against his people!Three Kings (criticizes) American hypocrisy alright, but in the most condescending way imaginable! Kinda like saying: "we as Americans are your gods, but sometimes we mock you, and that makes us bad gods"!!!In a nutshell: This film can be considered spoilers-free by dogs, blind cats and the below-average American Joe! If you're none of the above, don't waste a minute on it.</fullReview>

		<username>Jackson Booth-Millard</username>
		<score>0.8</score>
		<shortDescription>Three Kings</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>I didn't remember much about the actually story or events, so being put in the book 1001 Movies You Must See Before You Die was a good reason to see it again, from director David O. Russell (I Heart Huckabees). Basically it is 1991, and the end of the Gulf War, where four American soldiers have come across a secret map hidden in a man's arse, showing the whereabouts of a bunker in an Iraqi village. Major Archie Gates (George Clooney) is convinced that the hidden directions found are pointing to a huge stash of stolen gold bullion and treasure from Kuwait is being hidden, so they start the journey to find it. Archie, with companions Sergeant First Class Troy Barlow (Mark Wahlberg), Staff Sergeant Chief Elgin (Ice Cube) and Private First Class Conrad Vig (Being John Malkovich director Spike Jonze) hope to find the gold and keep it for themselves. To make sure that they will not have their plan spoilt, Archie gets Specialist Walter Wogaman (Scream's Jamie Kennedy) to get Emmy nominated journalist Adriana Cruz (Drop Dead Gorgeous's Nora Dunn) out the way with misdirection. They reach the village, and after being lied to that its in the next village, they go back and do eventually find the gold, and the Iraqi army do initially help them take it. But they soon have the hearts tested when the Iraqi army starts shooting and killing the innocent villagers and also taking prisoners, including Troy. Now Archie, Chief and Vig are working out a way to rescue Troy, and also help the many people facing certain death by Saddam Hussein and his military power. They do eventually manage to rescue Troy, and they strike a deal with Iraqi villager and ally Amir Abdulah (Die Hard 4.0's Cliff Curtis) to get all the villagers across the border to make sure they cannot be harmed any more. Also starring Forrest Gump's Mykelti Williamson as Colonel Horn and Judy Greer as Cathy Daitch. This is meant to be a comedy satire, it certainly does mock the period and the American army, it has a really good cast, some great action, good moments of gun play, and great small moments with special effects, a very worthwhile and most watchable wartime action adventure. George Clooney was number 72 on The 100 Greatest Movie Stars, and he was number 7 on The 100 Greatest Sex Symbols, and the film was number 50 on The 100 Greatest War Films. Very good!</fullReview>
	</review>
